<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Water buffalo</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">This article is about the domesticated water buffalo. For its endangered wild ancestor, see <a href="/wiki/Wild_water_buffalo" title="Wild water buffalo">Wild water buffalo</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Water_buffalo_(disambiguation)" title="Water buffalo (disambiguation)">Water buffalo (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p>The <b>water buffalo</b> or <b>domestic Asian water buffalo</b> (<i>Bubalus bubalis</i>) is a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bovid" title="Bovid">bovid</a> originating in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. Today, it is also found in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Wild_water_buffalo" title="Wild water buffalo">wild water buffalo</a> (<i>Bubalus arnee</i>) native to <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> is considered a different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Species_(biology)" title="Species (biology)">species</a>, but most likely represents the ancestor of the domestic water buffalo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two extant <a href="/wiki/Type_(biology)" title="Type (biology)">types</a> of water buffalo are recognized based on <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphological</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">behavioural</a> criteria – the <b>river buffalo</b> of South Asia and further west to the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and the <b>swamp buffalo</b>, found from <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> in the west through Southeast Asia to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze</a> valley of China in the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1974_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1974-3">[3]</a></sup> The origins of the domestic water buffalo types are debated, although results of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phylogenetic" title="Phylogenetic">phylogenetic</a> study indicate that the swamp type may have originated in China and was domesticated about 4,000 years ago, while the river type may have originated from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and was domesticated about 5,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Water buffalo were traded from the <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation" title="Indus Valley Civilisation">Indus Valley Civilisation</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, in modern <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, 2500 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Before_Christ" title="Before Christ">BC</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Meluhha" title="Meluhha">Meluhhas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The seal of a scribe employed by an <a href="/wiki/Akkadian" title="Akkadian">Akkadian</a> king shows the sacrifice of water buffalo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>At least 130 million domestic water buffalo exist, and more people depend on them than on any other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_animal" title="Domestic animal">domestic animal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> They are especially suitable for <a href="/wiki/Tillage" title="Tillage">tilling</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rice_field" title="Rice field">rice fields</a>, and their <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a> is richer in <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">protein</a> than that of <a href="/wiki/Dairy_cattle" title="Dairy cattle">dairy cattle</a>. The large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">feral</a> population of northern Australia became established in the late 19th century, and smaller feral herds are in <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, and northeastern <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup> Feral herds are also present in <a href="/wiki/New_Britain" title="New Britain">New Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Ireland_(island)" title="New Ireland (island)">New Ireland</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irian_Jaya" title="Irian Jaya">Irian Jaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Water_buffalo_skull_(Bubalus_bubalis).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2395" data-file-width="3577" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Water_buffalo_skull_%28Bubalus_bubalis%29.jpg/320px-Water_buffalo_skull_%28Bubalus_bubalis%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Water_buffalo_skull_%28Bubalus_bubalis%29.jpg/480px-Water_buffalo_skull_%28Bubalus_bubalis%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Water_buffalo_skull_%28Bubalus_bubalis%29.jpg/640px-Water_buffalo_skull_%28Bubalus_bubalis%29.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Water_Buffalo,_Phayao_Lake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1099" data-file-width="1500" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Water_Buffalo%2C_Phayao_Lake.jpg/220px-Water_Buffalo%2C_Phayao_Lake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Water_Buffalo%2C_Phayao_Lake.jpg/330px-Water_Buffalo%2C_Phayao_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Water_Buffalo%2C_Phayao_Lake.jpg/440px-Water_Buffalo%2C_Phayao_Lake.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Water_Buffalo,_Phayao_Lake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A water buffalo in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albino_Water_Buffalo,_Chiang_Mai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2572" data-file-width="3447" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Albino_Water_Buffalo%2C_Chiang_Mai.jpg/220px-Albino_Water_Buffalo%2C_Chiang_Mai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Albino_Water_Buffalo%2C_Chiang_Mai.jpg/330px-Albino_Water_Buffalo%2C_Chiang_Mai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Albino_Water_Buffalo%2C_Chiang_Mai.jpg/440px-Albino_Water_Buffalo%2C_Chiang_Mai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albino_Water_Buffalo,_Chiang_Mai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An albino swamp buffalo in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chiang_Mai_province" title="Chiang Mai province">Chiang Mai province</a>, Thailand</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The skin of river buffalo is black, but some specimens may have dark, slate-coloured skin. Swamp buffalo have a grey skin at birth, but become slate blue later. <a href="/wiki/Albinism" title="Albinism">Albinoids</a> are present in some populations. River buffalo have comparatively longer faces, smaller girths, and bigger limbs than swamp buffalo. Their dorsal ridges extend further back and taper off more gradually. Their horns grow downward and backward, then curve upward in a spiral. Swamp buffalo are heavy-bodied and stockily built; the body is short and the belly large. The forehead is flat, the eyes prominent, the face short, and the <a href="/wiki/Snout" title="Snout">muzzle</a> wide. The neck is comparatively long, and the <a href="/wiki/Withers" title="Withers">withers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rump_(animal)" title="Rump (animal)">croup</a> are prominent. A dorsal ridge extends backward and ends abruptly just before the end of the chest. Their horns grow outward, and curve in a semicircle, but always remain more or less on the plane of the forehead. The tail is short, reaching only to the <a href="/wiki/Hock_(anatomy)" title="Hock (anatomy)">hocks</a>. Height at withers is 129–133 cm (51–52 in) for males, and 120–127 cm (47–50 in) for females. They range in weight from 300–550 kg (660–1,210 lb), but weights of over 1,000 kg (2,200 lb) have also been observed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Tedong bonga</i> is a black pied buffalo featuring a unique black and white colouration that is favoured by the <a href="/wiki/Toraja" title="Toraja">Toraja</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The swamp buffalo has 48 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chromosomes" title="Chromosomes">chromosomes</a>; the river buffalo has 50 chromosomes. The two types do not readily interbreed, but fertile offspring can occur. Buffalo-<a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a> hybrids have not been observed to occur, but the embryos of such hybrids reach maturity in laboratory experiments, albeit at lower rates than non-hybrids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rumen" title="Rumen">rumen</a> of the water buffalo has important differences from that of other <a href="/wiki/Ruminant" title="Ruminant">ruminants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> It contains a larger population of <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>, particularly the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellulolytic" title="Cellulolytic">cellulolytic</a> bacteria, lower <a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoa</a>, and higher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">fungi</a> <a href="/wiki/Zoospore" title="Zoospore">zoospores</a>. In addition, higher rumen <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a> <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a> (NH<sub>4</sub>-N) and higher <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">pH</a> have been found as compared to those in <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology_and_behavior">Ecology and behavior</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ecology and behavior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Water_buffalo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="602" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Water_buffalo.jpg/220px-Water_buffalo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Water_buffalo.jpg/330px-Water_buffalo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Water_buffalo.jpg/440px-Water_buffalo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Water_buffalo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water buffalo enjoy being in water.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="676" data-file-width="1000" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Rainbirder_-_Water_Buffalo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water buffalo wallowing in mud</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>River buffalo prefer deep water. Swamp buffalo prefer to <a href="/wiki/Wallowing_in_animals" title="Wallowing in animals">wallow</a> in mudholes which they make with their horns. During wallowing, they acquire a thick coating of mud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup> Both are well adapted to a hot and humid climate with temperatures ranging from 0 °C (32 °F) in the winter to 30 °C (86 °F) and greater in the summer. Water availability is important in hot climates, since they need wallows, rivers, or splashing water to assist in <a href="/wiki/Thermoregulation" title="Thermoregulation">thermoregulation</a>. Some <a href="/wiki/Breed" title="Breed">breeds</a> are adapted to <a href="/wiki/Saline_water" title="Saline water">saline</a> seaside shores and <a href="/wiki/Soil_salinity" title="Soil salinity">saline sandy terrain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borghese2005_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Borghese2005-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diet">Diet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Diet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Water buffalo thrive on many <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_plant" title="Aquatic plant">aquatic plants</a> and during floods, will graze submerged, raising their heads above the water and carrying quantities of edible plants. They eat <a href="/wiki/Reed_(plant)" title="Reed (plant)">reeds</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Arundo_donax" title="Arundo donax">Arundo donax</a></i>, a kind of <i><a href="/wiki/Cyperaceae" title="Cyperaceae">Cyperaceae</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Eichhornia_crassipes" title="Eichhornia crassipes">Eichhornia crassipes</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Juncaceae" title="Juncaceae">Juncaceae</a></i>. Some of these plants are of great value to local peoples. Others, such as <i>E. crassipes</i>, are a major problem in some tropical valleys and water buffalo may help to keep waterways clear.</p>
<p>Green fodders are used widely for intensive milk production and for fattening. Many fodder crops are conserved as hay, chaffed, or pulped. Fodders include <a href="/wiki/Alfalfa" title="Alfalfa">alfalfa</a>, the leaves, stems or trimmings of <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mangelwurzel" title="Mangelwurzel">Mangelwurzel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esparto" title="Esparto">esparto</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Leucaena_leucocephala" title="Leucaena leucocephala">Leucaena leucocephala</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Kenaf" title="Kenaf">kenaf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oat" title="Oat">oats</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pandaros_(sponge)" title="Pandaros (sponge)">pandaros</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bagasse" title="Bagasse">bagasse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turnip" title="Turnip">turnips</a>. <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">Citrus</a> pulp and <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapple</a> wastes have been fed safely to buffalo. In Egypt, whole sun-dried <a href="/wiki/Date_palm#Dates" title="Date palm">dates</a> are fed to milk buffalo up to 25% of the standard feed mixture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reproduction">Reproduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Reproduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Water_buffalo_calf,_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Water_buffalo_calf%2C_India.jpg/220px-Water_buffalo_calf%2C_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Water_buffalo_calf%2C_India.jpg/330px-Water_buffalo_calf%2C_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Water_buffalo_calf%2C_India.jpg/440px-Water_buffalo_calf%2C_India.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Water_buffalo_calf,_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A water buffalo calf in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Swamp buffalo generally become <a href="/wiki/Reproduction" title="Reproduction">reproductive</a> at an older age than river breeds. Young males in Egypt, India, and Pakistan are first mated at about 3.0–3.5 years of age, but in Italy they may be used as early as 2 years of age. Successful mating behaviour may continue until the animal is 12 years or even older. A good river male can impregnate 100 females in a year. A strong seasonal influence on <a href="/wiki/Mating" title="Mating">mating</a> occurs. Heat stress reduces <a href="/wiki/Libido" title="Libido">libido</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although buffalo are polyoestrous, their reproductive efficiency shows wide variation throughout the year. Buffalo cows exhibit a distinct seasonal change in displaying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oestrus" title="Oestrus">oestrus</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conception_(biology)" title="Conception (biology)">conception</a> rate, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calf_(animal)" title="Calf (animal)">calving</a> rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barile2005_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barile2005-14">[14]</a></sup> The age at first oestrus of <a href="/wiki/Cattle#Terminology" title="Cattle">heifers</a> varies between breeds from 13–33 months, but mating at the first oestrus is often infertile and usually deferred until they are 3 years old. <a href="/wiki/Gestation" title="Gestation">Gestation</a> lasts from 281–334 days, but most reports give a range between 300 and 320 days. Swamp buffalo carry their calves for one or two weeks longer than river buffalo. It is not rare to find buffalo that continue to work well at the age of 30, and instances of a working life of 40 years are recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomic_history">Taxonomic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Taxonomic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:09963_Water_buffalo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2981" data-file-width="4472" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/09963_Water_buffalo.JPG/220px-09963_Water_buffalo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/09963_Water_buffalo.JPG/330px-09963_Water_buffalo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/09963_Water_buffalo.JPG/440px-09963_Water_buffalo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:09963_Water_buffalo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water buffalo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">Carl Linnaeus</a> first described the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Bos" title="Bos">Bos</a></i> and the water buffalo under the <a href="/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature" title="Binomial nomenclature">binomial</a> <i>Bubalis bubalus</i> in 1758; the latter was known to occur in Asia and as a domestic form in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Ellerman,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir John Ellerman, 1st Baronet">Ellerman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terence_Morrison-Scott" title="Terence Morrison-Scott">Morrison-Scott</a> treated the wild and domestic forms of the water buffalo as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conspecificity" title="Conspecificity">conspecifics</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> whereas others treated them as different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Species_(biology)" title="Species (biology)">species</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature" title="Binomial nomenclature">nomenclatorial</a> treatment of wild and domestic forms has been inconsistent and varies between authors and even within the works of single authors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2003, the <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_on_Zoological_Nomenclature" title="International Commission on Zoological Nomenclature">International Commission on Zoological Nomenclature</a> achieved consistency in the naming of wild and domestic water buffalo by ruling that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_name" title="Scientific name">scientific name</a> <i>Bubalus arnee</i> is valid for the wild form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <i>B. bubalis</i> continues to be valid for the domestic form and applies also to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">feral</a> populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestication_and_breeding">Domestication and breeding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Domestication and breeding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Murrah_buffalo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Murrah_buffalo.JPG/220px-Murrah_buffalo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Murrah_buffalo.JPG/330px-Murrah_buffalo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Murrah_buffalo.JPG/440px-Murrah_buffalo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Murrah_buffalo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Murrah buffalo at the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Carabao_Center" title="Philippine Carabao Center">Philippine Carabao Center</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Water buffalo were <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domesticated</a> in Indian subcontinent about 5000 years ago, and in China about 4000 years ago. Two types are recognized, based on <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphological</a> and behavioural criteria – the <b>river buffalo</b> of the Indian subcontinent and further west to the Balkans and Italy, and the <b>swamp buffalo</b>, found from Assam in the west through Southeast Asia to the Yangtze valley of China in the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1974_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1974-3">[3]</a></sup> The present-day river buffalo is the result of complex domestication processes involving more than one maternal lineage and a significant maternal <a href="/wiki/Gene_flow" title="Gene flow">gene flow</a> from wild populations after the initial domestication events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Twenty-two <a href="/wiki/Breed" title="Breed">breeds</a> of the river type water buffalo are known, including <a href="/wiki/Murrah_buffalo" title="Murrah buffalo">Murrah</a>, Nili-Ravi, <a href="/wiki/Surti_buffalo" title="Surti buffalo">Surti</a>, Jafarabadi, Anatolian, Mediterranean, and Egyptian buffalo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moioli2005_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moioli2005-22">[22]</a></sup> China has a huge variety of buffalo genetic resources, comprising 16 local swamp buffalo breeds in various regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borghese2005_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Borghese2005-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Results of <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA" title="Mitochondrial DNA">mitochondrial DNA</a> analyses indicate that the two types were domesticated independently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sequencing" title="Sequencing">Sequencing</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cytochrome_b" title="Cytochrome b">cytochrome b</a> <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> of <i>Bubalus</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Species_(biology)" title="Species (biology)">species</a> implies that the domestic buffalo originated from at least two populations, and that the river and the swamp types have differentiated at the full species level. The <a href="/wiki/Genetic_distance" title="Genetic distance">genetic distance</a> between the two types is so large that a divergence time of about 1.7 million years has been suggested. The swamp type was noticed to have the closest relationship with the <a href="/wiki/Tamaraw" title="Tamaraw">tamaraw</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution_of_populations">Distribution of populations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Distribution of populations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Philippine_Carabao.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Philippine_Carabao.jpg/220px-Philippine_Carabao.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Philippine_Carabao.jpg/330px-Philippine_Carabao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Philippine_Carabao.jpg/440px-Philippine_Carabao.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Philippine_Carabao.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Carabao" title="Carabao">Carabao</a> buffalo in the Philippines</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The water buffalo population in the world is about 172 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borghese2011_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Borghese2011-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Asia">In Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: In Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carabao_Cart.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2302" data-file-width="3000" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Carabao_Cart.jpg/220px-Carabao_Cart.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Carabao_Cart.jpg/330px-Carabao_Cart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Carabao_Cart.jpg/440px-Carabao_Cart.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carabao_Cart.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carabao cart in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> in 1899</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>More than 95.8% of the world population of water buffalo are found in Asia, including both river and swamp types.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borghese2005_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Borghese2005-13">[13]</a></sup> The water buffalo population in India numbered over 97.9 million head in 2003, representing 56.5% of the world population. They are primarily of the river type, with 10 well-defined breeds comprising Badhawari, Murrah, Nili-Ravi, Jafarabadi, Marathwada, Mehsana, Nagpuri, Pandharpuri, Toda, and Surti. Swamp buffalo occur only in small areas in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_India" title="Northeast India">north-eastern part of the country</a> and are not distinguished into breeds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh2010_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Singh2010-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, the second-largest population lived in China, with 22.76 million head, all of the swamp type with breeds kept only in the lowlands, and other breeds kept only in the mountains; as of 2003, 3.2 million swamp-type <a href="/wiki/Carabao" title="Carabao">carabao</a> buffalo were in the Philippines, nearly three million swamp buffalo were in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, and 772,764 buffalo were in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>. About 750,000 head were estimated in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borghese2005_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-Borghese2005-13">[13]</a></sup> In Japan, water buffalo is domestic animal throughout the Ryukyuan islands or Okinawa prefecture.</p>
<p>The water buffalo is the main dairy animal in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, with 23.47 million head in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Of these, 76% are kept in the <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab</a>. The rest of them are mostly in the province of <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a>. Breeds used are <a href="/wiki/Niliravi" title="Niliravi">Niliravi</a>, Kundi, and Azi Kheli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a> has the largest population of water buffalos for an area where fodder is not grown, consisting of 350,000 head kept mainly for milking.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, the number of water buffalo dropped from more than 3 million head in 1996 to less than 1.24 million head in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Slightly over 75% of them are kept in the country's northeastern region. The statistics also indicate that by the beginning of 2012, less than one million were in the country, partly as a result of illegal shipments to neighboring countries where sales prices are higher than in Thailand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Water buffalo are also present in the southern region of <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_Marshes" title="Mesopotamian Marshes">Mesopotamian Marshes</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Draining_of_the_Mesopotamian_Marshes" title="Draining of the Mesopotamian Marshes">draining of the Mesopotamian Marshes</a> by <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> was an attempt to punish the south for the <a href="/wiki/1991_uprisings_in_Iraq" title="1991 uprisings in Iraq">1991 uprisings in Iraq</a>. After 2003 and the <a href="/wiki/Firdos_Square_statue_destruction" title="Firdos Square statue destruction">Firdos Square statue destruction</a>, these lands were reflooded and a 2007 report on <a href="/wiki/Maysan_Governorate" title="Maysan Governorate">Maysan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhi_Qar_Governorate" title="Dhi Qar Governorate">Dhi Qar</a> shows a steady increase in the number of water buffalo. The report puts the number at 40,008 head in those two provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Europe_and_the_Mediterranean">In Europe and the Mediterranean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: In Europe and the Mediterranean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Water buffalo were probably introduced to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> from India or other <a href="/wiki/Orient" title="Orient">Oriental</a> countries. In <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Longobard" title="Longobard">Longobard</a> King <a href="/wiki/Agilulf" title="Agilulf">Agilulf</a> is said to have received water buffalo in about the year 600. These were probably a present from the <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Khan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkic_people" title="Turkic people">Turkic</a> nomadic tribe that dwelt near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danube_River" title="Danube River">Danube River</a> at the time. <a href="/wiki/Harry_Johnston" title="Harry Johnston">Sir H. Johnston</a> knew of a herd of water buffalo presented by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Naples" title="King of Naples">King of Naples</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bey_of_Tunis" title="Bey of Tunis">Bey of Tunis</a> in the mid-19th century that had resumed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">feral</a> state in northern <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>European buffalo are all of the river type and considered to be of the same breed named Mediterranean buffalo. In Italy, the Mediterranean type was particularly selected and is called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranea_Italiana" title="Mediterranea Italiana">Mediterranean Italian breed</a> to distinguish it from other European breeds, which differ genetically. Mediterranean buffalo are also found in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, with a few hundred in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>. Little exchange of breeding buffalo has occurred among countries, so each population has its own <a href="/wiki/Phenotype" title="Phenotype">phenotypic</a> features and performances. In Bulgaria, they were crossbred with the Indian Murrah breed, and in Romania, some were crossbred with Bulgarian Murrah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borghese2005_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-Borghese2005-13">[13]</a></sup> Populations in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> are of the Anatolian buffalo breed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moioli2005_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Moioli2005-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Australia">In Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: In Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WildWaterBuffalo(Bubalus_bubalis_arnee).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="510" data-file-width="800" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/WildWaterBuffalo%28Bubalus_bubalis_arnee%29.jpg/220px-WildWaterBuffalo%28Bubalus_bubalis_arnee%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/WildWaterBuffalo%28Bubalus_bubalis_arnee%29.jpg/330px-WildWaterBuffalo%28Bubalus_bubalis_arnee%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/WildWaterBuffalo%28Bubalus_bubalis_arnee%29.jpg/440px-WildWaterBuffalo%28Bubalus_bubalis_arnee%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WildWaterBuffalo(Bubalus_bubalis_arnee).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A feral water buffalo in Australia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1824 and 1849, water buffalo were introduced into the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> from <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kisar" title="Kisar">Kisar</a>, and probably other islands in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indonesian_archipelago" title="Indonesian archipelago">Indonesian archipelago</a>. In 1886, a few milking types were brought from India to <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Northern_Territory" title="Darwin, Northern Territory">Darwin</a>. They have been the main grazing animals on the subcoastal plains and river basins between Darwin and <a href="/wiki/Arnhem_Land" title="Arnhem Land">Arnhem Land</a> since the 1880s. In the early 1960s, an estimated population of 150,000 to 200,000 buffalo were living in the plains and nearby areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>They became feral and are causing significant environmental damage. Buffalo are also found in the <a href="/wiki/Top_End" title="Top End">Top End</a>. As a result, they were hunted in the Top End from 1885 until 1980. The commencement of the <a href="/wiki/Brucellosis" title="Brucellosis">brucellosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> campaign (BTEC) resulted in a huge culling program to reduce buffalo herds to a fraction of the numbers that were reached in the 1980s. The BTEC was finished when the Northern Territory was declared free of the disease in 1997. Numbers dropped dramatically as a result of the campaign, but have since recovered to an estimated 150,000 animals across northern Australia in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1950s, buffalo were hunted for their skins and meat, which was exported and used in the local trade. In the late 1970s, live exports were made to <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and continued later into other countries. Buffalo are now crossed with riverine buffalo in <a href="/wiki/Artificial_insemination" title="Artificial insemination">artificial insemination</a> programs, and may be found in many areas of Australia. Some of these <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crossbred" title="Crossbred">crossbreds</a> are used for milk production. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melville_Island_(Northern_Territory)" title="Melville Island (Northern Territory)">Melville Island</a> is a popular hunting location, where a steady population up to 4,000 individuals exists. Safari outfits are run from <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Northern_Territory" title="Darwin, Northern Territory">Darwin</a> to Melville Island and other locations in the Top End, often with the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bush_pilot" title="Bush pilot">bush pilots</a>. The horns, which can measure up to a record of 3.1 m (10 ft) tip-to-tip, are prized hunting trophies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sharp_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sharp-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The buffalo have developed a different appearance from the Indonesian buffalo from which they descend.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They live mainly in freshwater marshes and <a href="/wiki/Billabong" title="Billabong">billabongs</a>, and their territory range can be quite expansive during the <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a>. Their only natural predators in Australia are adult <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">saltwater crocodiles</a>, with whom they share the billabongs, and <a href="/wiki/Dingo" title="Dingo">dingoes</a>, which have been known to prey on buffalo calves and occasionally adult buffalo when the dingoes are in large packs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Buffalo were exported live to Indonesia until 2011, at a rate of about 3000 per year. After the live export ban that year, the exports dropped to zero, and had not resumed as of June 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_South_America">In South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: In South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG/220px-B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG/330px-B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG/440px-B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B%C3%BAfalo_Murrah.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Murrah buffalo in a Brazilian Farm</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Water buffalo were introduced into the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a> basin in 1895. They are now extensively used there for meat and dairy production. In 2005, the buffalo herd in the <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> Amazon stood at roughly 1.6 million head, of which 460,000 were located in the lower Amazon floodplain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Breeds used include Mediterranean from Italy, Murrah and Jafarabadi from India, and Carabao from the Philippines.</p>
<p>During the 1970s, small herds were imported to <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayenne" title="Cayenne">Cayenne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surinam" title="Surinam">Surinam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRC-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Argentina, many game ranches raise water buffalo for commercial hunting.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_North_America">In North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: In North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1974, four water buffalo were imported to the United States from <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> to be studied at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">University of Florida</a>. In February 1978, the first herd arrived for commercial farming. Until 2002, only one commercial breeder was in the United States. Water buffalo meat is imported from Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRC_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-NRC-37">[37]</a></sup> Until 2011, water buffalo were raised in <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville, Florida</a>, from young obtained from zoo overflow. They were used primarily for meat production, frequently sold as hamburger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Other US ranchers use them for production of high-quality <a href="/wiki/Mozzarella" title="Mozzarella">mozzarella</a> cheese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Husbandry">Husbandry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Husbandry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KerbauJawa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="991" data-file-width="1500" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/KerbauJawa.jpg/220px-KerbauJawa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/KerbauJawa.jpg/330px-KerbauJawa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/KerbauJawa.jpg/440px-KerbauJawa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KerbauJawa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water buffalo ploughing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rice_fields" title="Rice fields">rice fields</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Java_(island)" title="Java (island)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Child_and_ox_ploughing,_Laos_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1708" data-file-width="2616" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Child_and_ox_ploughing%2C_Laos_%281%29.jpg/220px-Child_and_ox_ploughing%2C_Laos_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Child_and_ox_ploughing%2C_Laos_%281%29.jpg/330px-Child_and_ox_ploughing%2C_Laos_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Child_and_ox_ploughing%2C_Laos_%281%29.jpg/440px-Child_and_ox_ploughing%2C_Laos_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Child_and_ox_ploughing,_Laos_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water buffalo are used for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ploughing" title="Ploughing">ploughing</a> in <a href="/wiki/Si_Phan_Don" title="Si Phan Don">Si Phan Don</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="844" data-file-width="1280" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg/220px-Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg/330px-Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg/440px-Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yuanyang_cow_pat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cow_dung" title="Cow dung">Water buffalo dung</a> is dried against the façade of a house in <a href="/wiki/Yuanyang_County,_Yunnan" title="Yuanyang County, Yunnan">Yuanyang County, Yunnan</a>, China</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The husbandry system of water buffalo depends on the purpose for which they are bred and maintained. Most of them are kept by people who work on small farms in family units. Their buffalo live in very close association with them, and are often their greatest <a href="/wiki/Capital_asset" title="Capital asset">capital asset</a>. The women and girls in India generally look after the milking buffalo while the men and boys are concerned with the working animals. Throughout Asia, they are commonly tended by children who are often seen leading or riding their charges to wallowing places. Water buffalo are the ideal animals for work in the deep mud of <a href="/wiki/Paddy_field" title="Paddy field">paddy fields</a> because of their large hooves and flexible foot joints. They are often referred to as "the living tractor of the East". It probably is possible to plough deeper with buffalo than with either oxen or horses. They are the most efficient and economical means of cultivation of small fields. In most rice-producing countries, they are used for threshing and for transporting the <a href="/wiki/Sheaf_(agriculture)" title="Sheaf (agriculture)">sheaves</a> during the rice harvest. They provide power for oilseed mills, sugarcane presses, and devices for raising water. They are widely used as <a href="/wiki/Pack_animal" title="Pack animal">pack animals</a>, and in India and Pakistan also for heavy haulage. In their invasions of Europe, the Turks used buffalo for hauling heavy battering rams. Their dung is used as a <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizer</a>, and as a <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a> when dried.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cockrill1977_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-Cockrill1977-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Buffalo contribute 72 million tones of <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a> and three million tones of <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a> annually to world food, much of it in areas that are prone to nutritional imbalances. In India, river-type buffalo are kept mainly for milk production and for transport, whereas swamp-type buffalo are kept mainly for work and a small amount of milk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh2010_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Singh2010-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dairy_products">Dairy products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Dairy products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pccmilkjf.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Pccmilkjf.JPG/220px-Pccmilkjf.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Pccmilkjf.JPG/330px-Pccmilkjf.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Pccmilkjf.JPG/440px-Pccmilkjf.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pccmilkjf.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dairy products of water buffalo milk</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Water buffalo milk presents physicochemical features different from that of other <a href="/wiki/Ruminant" title="Ruminant">ruminant</a> species, such as a higher content of <a href="/wiki/Fatty_acid" title="Fatty acid">fatty acids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">proteins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The physical and chemical parameters of swamp and river type water buffalo milk differ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Water buffalo milk contains higher levels of total solids, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_protein" title="Crude protein">crude protein</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milk_fat" title="Milk fat">fat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">calcium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">phosphorus</a>, and slightly higher content of <a href="/wiki/Lactose" title="Lactose">lactose</a> compared with those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cow_milk" title="Cow milk">cow milk</a>. The high level of total solids makes water buffalo milk ideal for processing into value-added dairy products such as <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheese</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Conjugated_linoleic_acid" title="Conjugated linoleic acid">conjugated linoleic acid</a> (CLA) content in milk ranged from 4.4 mg/g fat in September to 7.6 mg/g fat in June. Seasons and genetics may play a role in variation of CLA level and changes in gross composition of the water buffalo milk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Water buffalo milk is processed into a large variety of <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cream" title="Cream">Cream</a> <a href="/wiki/Churning_(butter)" title="Churning (butter)">churns</a> much faster at higher fat levels and gives higher overrun than cow cream.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Butter" title="Butter">Butter</a> from water buffalo cream displays more stability than that from cow cream.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ghee" title="Ghee">Ghee</a> from water buffalo milk has a different texture with a bigger grain size than ghee from cow milk.</li>
<li>Heat-concentrated milk products in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> include <i><a href="/wiki/Paneer" title="Paneer">paneer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khoa" title="Khoa">khoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabri" title="Rabri">rabri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kheer" title="Kheer">kheer</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Basundi" title="Basundi">basundi</a></i>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermented_milk" title="Fermented milk">Fermented milk</a> products include <i>dahi</i>, <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Strained_yogurt" title="Strained yogurt">chakka</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Whey" title="Whey">Whey</a> is used for making <a href="/wiki/Ricotta" title="Ricotta">ricotta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mascarpone" title="Mascarpone">mascarpone</a> in Italy, and <i>alkarish</i> in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and Egypt.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soft_cheese" title="Soft cheese">Soft cheeses</a> made include mozzarella in Italy, <i>karish</i>, <i>mish</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Domiati" title="Domiati">domiati</a> in Egypt, <i>madhfor</i> in Iraq, <i>alghab</i> in Syria, <i>kesong puti</i> in the Philippines, and <i>vladeasa</i> in Romania.</li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Semihard_cheese&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Semihard cheese (page does not exist)">semihard cheese</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Beyaz_peynir" title="Beyaz peynir">beyaz peynir</a></i> is made in Turkey.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hard_cheese" title="Hard cheese">Hard cheeses</a> include <i>braila</i> in Romania, <i>rahss</i> in Egypt,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> <i>white brine</i> in Bulgaria, and <i><a href="/wiki/Akkawi" title="Akkawi">akkawi</a></i> in Syria.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toned_milk" title="Toned milk">Watered-down buffalo milk</a> is used as a cheaper alternative to regular milk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dairyall_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-dairyall-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
