<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meat_and_skin_products">Meat and skin products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Meat and skin products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_meat" title="Buffalo meat">Buffalo meat</a></div>
<p>Water buffalo meat, sometimes called "carabeef", is often passed off as beef in certain regions, and is also a major source of export revenue for India. In many Asian regions, buffalo meat is less preferred due to its toughness; however, recipes have evolved (<i><a href="/wiki/Rendang" title="Rendang">rendang</a></i>, for example) where the slow cooking process and spices not only make the meat palatable, but also preserve it, an important factor in hot climates where refrigeration is not always available.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Their hides provide tough and useful <a href="/wiki/Leather" title="Leather">leather</a>, often used for shoes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bone_and_horn_products">Bone and horn products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Bone and horn products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="672" data-file-width="559" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg/220px-Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg/330px-Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg/440px-Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bihu_dancer_with_a_horn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Bihu" title="Bihu">bihu</a> dancer is blowing a <a href="/wiki/Hornpipe_(instrument)" title="Hornpipe (instrument)">hornpipe</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The bones and horns are often made into jewellery, especially earrings. Horns are used for the embouchure of musical instruments, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Ney" title="Ney">ney</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kaval" title="Kaval">kaval</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_effects">Environmental effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environmental effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wildlife_conservation" title="Wildlife conservation">Wildlife conservation</a> scientists have started to recommend and use introduced populations of feral domestic water buffalo in far-away lands to manage uncontrolled vegetation growth in and around natural <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a>. Introduced water buffalo at home in such environs provide cheap service by regularly grazing the uncontrolled vegetation and opening up clogged water bodies for <a href="/wiki/Waterfowl" title="Waterfowl">waterfowl</a>, wetland birds, and other wildlife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Grazing water buffalo are sometimes used in <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> for <a href="/wiki/Conservation_grazing" title="Conservation grazing">conservation grazing</a>, such as in Chippenham Fen National Nature Reserve. The buffalo can better adapt to wet conditions and poor-quality vegetation than cattle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Currently, research is being conducted at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lyle_Center_for_Regenerative_Studies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lyle Center for Regenerative Studies (page does not exist)">Lyle Center for Regenerative Studies</a> to determine the levels of nutrients removed and returned to wetlands when water buffalo are used for wetland vegetation management.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>However, in uncontrolled circumstances, water buffalo can cause environmental damage, such as trampling vegetation, disturbing bird and reptile nesting sites, and spreading exotic weeds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roth.2C_J._and_P._Myers_2004_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roth.2C_J._and_P._Myers_2004-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pcc22jf.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Pcc22jf.JPG/220px-Pcc22jf.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Pcc22jf.JPG/330px-Pcc22jf.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Pcc22jf.JPG/440px-Pcc22jf.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pcc22jf.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The super carabaos at the milking and breeding station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The world's first <a href="/wiki/Cloning" title="Cloning">cloned</a> buffalo was developed by Indian scientists from <a href="/wiki/National_Dairy_Research_Institute" title="National Dairy Research Institute">National Dairy Research Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karnal" title="Karnal">Karnal</a>. The buffalo calf was named Samrupa. The calf did not survive more than a week, and died due to some genetic disorders. So, the scientists created another cloned buffalo a few months later, and named it Garima.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 September 2007, the Philippines announced its development of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>'s first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cloned" title="Cloned">cloned</a> buffalo. The Philippine Council for Agriculture, Forestry and Natural Resources Research and Development (PCARRD), under the Department of Science and Technology in <a href="/wiki/Los_Ba%C3%B1os,_Laguna" title="Los Baños, Laguna">Los Baños, Laguna</a>, approved this project. The Department of Agriculture's Philippine Carabao Center (PCC) will implement cloning through somatic cell nuclear transfer as a tool for genetic improvement in water buffalo. "Super buffalo calves" will be produced. There will be no modification or alteration of the <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genetic</a> materials, as in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organisms" title="Genetically modified organisms">genetically modified organisms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 January 2008, the Philippine Carabao Center in <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Ecija" title="Nueva Ecija">Nueva Ecija</a>, per <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_people" title="Filipino people">Filipino</a> scientists, initiated a study to breed a super water buffalo that could produce 4 to 18 litres of milk per day using gene-based technology. Also, the first <i>in vitro</i> river buffalo was born there in 2004 from an <i>in vitro</i>-produced, vitrified embryo, named "Glory" after President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo" title="Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Estrada" title="Joseph Estrada">Joseph Estrada</a>'s most successful project as an opposition senator, the PCC was created through Republic Act 3707, the Carabao Act of 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_culture">In culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: In culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1088" data-file-width="1399" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg/220px-WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg/330px-WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg/440px-WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WaterBuffaloLopburiThailand2300BCE.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ceramic water buffalo from 2300 BC found in <a href="/wiki/Lopburi" title="Lopburi">Lopburi</a>, Thailand</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yama_on_buffalo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="687" data-file-width="640" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Yama_on_buffalo.jpg/220px-Yama_on_buffalo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Yama_on_buffalo.jpg/330px-Yama_on_buffalo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Yama_on_buffalo.jpg/440px-Yama_on_buffalo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yama_on_buffalo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hindu god Yama (god of death) on a buffalo</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Water_Buffalo_by_Hokusai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="417" height="317" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Water_Buffalo_by_Hokusai.jpg/220px-Water_Buffalo_by_Hokusai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Water_Buffalo_by_Hokusai.jpg/330px-Water_Buffalo_by_Hokusai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/94/Water_Buffalo_by_Hokusai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Water_Buffalo_by_Hokusai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water Buffalo (Suigyū) by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Katsushika_Hokusai" title="Katsushika Hokusai">Katsushika Hokusai</a>, <i>circa</i> 1875</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Tijdens_het_slepen_van_een_grafsteen_wordt_even_uitgerust_op_de_steen_zijn_horens_van_de_geofferde_karbouwen_gebonden_West-Sumba%27_TMnr_10003262.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="498" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Tijdens_het_slepen_van_een_grafsteen_wordt_even_uitgerust_op_de_steen_zijn_horens_van_de_geofferde_karbouwen_gebonden_West-Sumba%27_TMnr_10003262.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Tijdens_het_slepen_van_een_grafsteen_wordt_even_uitgerust_op_de_steen_zijn_horens_van_de_geofferde_karbouwen_gebonden_West-Sumba%27_TMnr_10003262.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Tijdens_het_slepen_van_een_grafsteen_wordt_even_uitgerust_op_de_steen_zijn_horens_van_de_geofferde_karbouwen_gebonden_West-Sumba%27_TMnr_10003262.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Tijdens_het_slepen_van_een_grafsteen_wordt_even_uitgerust_op_de_steen_zijn_horens_van_de_geofferde_karbouwen_gebonden_West-Sumba%27_TMnr_10003262.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Horns of water buffalo sacrificed in <a href="/wiki/West_Sumba_Regency" title="West Sumba Regency">West Sumba</a>, Indonesia, <i>circa</i> 1936 (collection <a href="/wiki/Tropenmuseum" title="Tropenmuseum">Tropenmuseum</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Some ethnic groups, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batak_(Indonesia)" title="Batak (Indonesia)">Batak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toraja" title="Toraja">Toraja</a> in Indonesia and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Derung" title="Derung">Derung</a> in China, sacrifice water buffalo or <i>kerbau</i> (called <i>horbo</i> in Batak or <i>tedong</i> in Toraja) at several festivals.</li>
<li>Legend has it that the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_philosophy" title="Chinese philosophy">Chinese philosophical</a> sage <a href="/wiki/Laozi" title="Laozi">Laozi</a> left China through the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Han_Gu_Pass&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Han Gu Pass (page does not exist)">Han Gu Pass</a> riding a water buffalo.</li>
<li>According to <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> lore, the god of death <a href="/wiki/Yama_(Hinduism)" title="Yama (Hinduism)">Yama</a>, rides on a male water buffalo. The Hindu goddesses Varahi and Vihot Mata also ride on buffalo as their <a href="/wiki/Vahana" title="Vahana">vahana</a>.</li>
<li>According to another folk lore, <a href="/wiki/Mahishasura" title="Mahishasura">Mahishasura</a>, a half-buffalo and half-human demon, was killed by goddess <a href="/wiki/Durga" title="Durga">Durga</a>.</li>
<li>The Yoruban Orisha Oya (goddess of change) takes the form of a water buffalo.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Carabao" title="Carabao">carabao</a> breed is considered a <a href="/wiki/National_symbol" title="National symbol">national symbol</a> of the Philippines.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, water buffalo are often the most valuable possession of poor farmers: 'Con trâu là đầu cơ nghiệp'. They are treated as a member of the family: 'Chồng cày, vợ cấy, con trâu đi bừa', meaning 'the husband ploughs, the wife sows, water buffalo draws the rake'. Children talk to their water buffalo: 'Bao giờ cây lúa còn bông. Thì còn ngọn cỏ ngoài đồng trâu ăn'. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H%C3%A0_N%E1%BB%99i" title="Hà Nội">Hà Nội</a> used to be named Kim Ngưu - Golden Water Buffalo.</li>
<li>Many ethnic groups use the horn of water buffalo as a game trophy, musical instruments and ornaments.</li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Burmese_zodiac#Weekdays" title="Burmese zodiac">Thai and Sinhalese animal and planetary zodiac</a>, the buffalo is the sixth animal zodiac of the <a href="/wiki/Thai_people" title="Thai people">Thai</a> and the fourth animal zodiac of the <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_people" title="Sinhalese people">Sinhalese people</a> of Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Water_buffalo_(zodiac)" title="Water buffalo (zodiac)">water buffalo</a> is the second animal zodiac in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_zodiac" title="Chinese zodiac">Vietnamese zodiac</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fighting_festivals">Fighting festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Fighting festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg/220px-Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg/330px-Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg/440px-Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Water_Buffalo_fight.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An unstaged water buffalo fight</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Pasungay Festival is held annually in the town of <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin,_Iloilo" title="San Joaquin, Iloilo">San Joaquin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iloilo" title="Iloilo">Iloilo</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.</li>
<li>Moh juj Water Buffalo fighting is held every year in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bhogali_Bihu" title="Bhogali Bihu">Bhogali Bihu</a> in <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Ahotguri in <a href="/wiki/Nagaon" title="Nagaon">Nagaon</a> is famous for it.</li>
<li>Do Son Water Buffalo Fighting Festival of Vietnam is held each year on the ninth day of the eighth month of the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_calendar" title="Lunar calendar">lunar calendar</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Do_Son" title="Do Son">Do Son</a> Township, <a href="/wiki/Haiphong" title="Haiphong">Haiphong</a> City in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. It is one of the most popular Vietnam festivals and events in Haiphong City. The preparations for this buffalo fighting festival begin from the two to three months earlier. The competing buffalo are selected and methodically trained months in advance. It is a traditional festival of Vietnam attached to a Water God worshipping ceremony and the <i>Hien Sinh</i> custom to show martial spirit of the local people of Do Son, Haiphong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Hai Luu" Water Buffalo Fighting Festival of Vietnam has existed since the 2nd century B.C. General Lu Gia at that time, had the buffalo slaughtered to give a feast to the local people and the warriors, and organized buffalo fighting for amusement. Eventually, all the fighting buffalo will be slaughtered as tributes to the deities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Ko Samui" Water Buffalo Fighting Festival of Thailand is a very popular event held on special occasions such as New Year's Day in January, and Songkran in mid-April, this festival features head-wrestling bouts in which two male Asian water buffalo are pitted against one another. Unlike in Spanish Bullfighting, wherein bulls get killed while fighting sword-wielding men, Buffalo Fighting Festival held at <a href="/wiki/Ko_Samui" title="Ko Samui">Ko Samui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> is fairly harmless contest. The fighting season varies according to ancient customs &amp; ceremonies. The first Buffalo to turn and run away is considered the loser, the winning buffalo becomes worth several million baht.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Ma'Pasilaga Tedong" Water Buffalo Fighting Festival, in <a href="/wiki/Tana_Toraja_Regency" title="Tana Toraja Regency">Tana Toraja Regency</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sulawesi_Island" title="Sulawesi Island">Sulawesi Island</a>, Indonesia, is a popular event where the Rambu Solo or a Burial Festival took place in Tana Toraja.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Racing_festivals">Racing festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Racing festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bisbuffalorace.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="311" data-file-width="568" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Bisbuffalorace.jpg/220px-Bisbuffalorace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Bisbuffalorace.jpg/330px-Bisbuffalorace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Bisbuffalorace.jpg/440px-Bisbuffalorace.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bisbuffalorace.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water buffalo racing at <a href="/wiki/Babulang" title="Babulang">Babulang</a> 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kambala,_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village,_Udupi_Dist.,_Kar._India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/Kambala%2C_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village%2C_Udupi_Dist.%2C_Kar._India.jpg/220px-Kambala%2C_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village%2C_Udupi_Dist.%2C_Kar._India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/Kambala%2C_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village%2C_Udupi_Dist.%2C_Kar._India.jpg/330px-Kambala%2C_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village%2C_Udupi_Dist.%2C_Kar._India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/Kambala%2C_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village%2C_Udupi_Dist.%2C_Kar._India.jpg/440px-Kambala%2C_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village%2C_Udupi_Dist.%2C_Kar._India.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kambala,_he-buffalo_race_at_Vandar_village,_Udupi_Dist.,_Kar._India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buffalo race at Vandar village, <a href="/wiki/Udupi_district" title="Udupi district">Udupi district</a>, India.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Carabao Carroza Festival is being held annually every May in the town of <a href="/wiki/Pavia,_Iloilo" title="Pavia, Iloilo">Pavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iloilo" title="Iloilo">Iloilo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kambala" title="Kambala">Kambala</a> races of <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, take place between December and March. The races are conducted by having the water buffalo (he buffalo) run in long parallel slushy ditches, where they are driven by men standing on wooden planks drawn by the buffalo. The objectives of the race are to finish first and to raise the water to the greatest height and also a rural sport. Kambala races are arranged with competition, as well as without competition and as a part of thanks giving (to god) in about 50 villages of coastal Karnataka.</li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Chonburi_Province" title="Chonburi Province">Chonburi Province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, there are annual water buffalo races.</li>
<li>Chon Buri Water buffalo racing festival, Thailand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In downtown <a href="/wiki/Chonburi_(city)" title="Chonburi (city)">Chonburi</a>, 70 km (43 mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, at the annual water buffalo festival held in mid-October. About 300 buffalo race in groups of five or six, spurred on by bareback jockeys wielding wooden sticks, as hundreds of spectators cheer. The water buffalo has always played an important role in agriculture in Thailand. For farmers of Chon Buri Province, near Bangkok, it is an important annual festival, beginning in mid-October. It is also a celebration among rice farmers before the rice harvest. At dawn, farmers walk their buffalo through surrounding rice fields, splashing them with water to keep them cool before leading them to the race field. This amazing festival started over a hundred years ago when two men arguing about whose buffalo was the fastest ended up having a race between them. That’s how it became a tradition and gradually a social event for farmers who gathered from around the country in Chonburi to trade their goods. The festival also helps a great deal in preserving the number of buffalo, which have been dwindling at quite an alarming rate in other regions. Modern machinery is rapidly replacing buffalo in Thai agriculture. With most of the farm work mechanized, the buffalo-racing tradition has continued. Racing buffalo are now raised just to race; they do not work at all. The few farm buffalo which still do work are much bigger than the racers because of the strenuous work they perform. Farm buffalo are in the "Buffalo Beauty Pageant", a Miss Farmer beauty contest and a comic buffalo costume contest etc.. This festival perfectly exemplifies a favored Thai attitude to life — "sanuk," meaning fun.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Babulang" title="Babulang">Babulang</a> Water buffalo racing festival in <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, Malaysia, is the largest or grandest of the many rituals, ceremonies and festivals of the traditional <a href="/wiki/Bisaya_(Borneo)" title="Bisaya (Borneo)">Bisaya</a> community of Limbang, Sarawak. Highlights are the Ratu Babulang competition and the Water buffalo races which can only be found in this town in <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.</li>
<li>Vihear Suor village Water buffalo racing festival, Cambodia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> each year, people visit Buddhist temples across the country to honor their deceased loved ones during a 15-day period commonly known as the <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_the_Dead" title="Festival of the Dead">Festival of the Dead</a> but in Vihear Suor village, about 22 miles (35 km) northeast of Cambodia, citizens each year wrap up the festival with a water buffalo race to entertain visitors and honour a pledge made hundreds of years ago. There was a time when many village cattle which provide rural Cambodians with muscle power to plough their fields and transport agricultural products died from an unknown disease. The villagers prayed to a spirit to help save their animals from the disease and promised to show their gratitude by holding a buffalo race each year on the last day of "P'chum Ben" festival as it is known in Cambodian. The race draws hundreds of spectators who come to see riders and their animals charge down the racing field, the racers bouncing up and down on the backs of their buffalo, whose horns were draped with colorful cloth.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buffalo_racing_in_Kerala" title="Buffalo racing in Kerala">Buffalo racing in Kerala</a> is similar to <a href="/wiki/Kambala" title="Kambala">Kambala</a> races.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_festival">Religious festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_buffalo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Religious festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The Pulilan Carabao Festival is held annually every 14 and 15 May in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippine</a> town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulilan" title="Pulilan">Pulilan</a> in honor of <a href="/wiki/Isidore_the_Laborer" title="Isidore the Laborer">St. Isidore the Laborer</a>, the patron saint of farmers. As thanksgiving for a bountiful harvest every year, farmers parade their carabaos in the main town street, adorning them with garlands and other decorations. One of the highlights of the festival is the kneeling of the carabaos in front of the parish church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<li>Fahimuddin, M. 1989. <i>Domestic Water Buffalo</i>. Janpath, New Delhi: Oxford &amp; IBH Publishing Co. Pvt. Ltd. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/8120404025">ISBN 81-204-0402-5</a>.</li>
<li>The Water Buffalo: New Prospects For An Underutilized Animal. Washington, D.C. 1981. National Academy Press. <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780309041591">ISBN 978-0-309-04159-1</a>.</li>
<li>Wilson, D. E. and Reeder, D. M. 1993. <i>Mammal Species of the World, Second Edition, A Taxonomic and Geographic Reference</i>. Smithsonian Institution.</li>
<li>Ruangprim, T. et al. 2007. Rumen microbes and ecology of male dairy, beef cattle and buffaloes. In: Proceedings Animal Science Annual Meeting, Khon Kaen University, Khon Kaen 40002, Thailand.</li>
<li>Thu, Nguyen Van and T. R. Preston. 1999. Rumen environment and feed degradability in swamp buffaloes fed different supplements. Livestock Research for Rural Development 11 (3)</li>
<li>Wanapat, M. 2000. Rumen manipulation to increase the efficient use of local feed resources and productivity of ruminants in the tropics. Asian-Aust. J. Anim. Sci. 13(Suppl.): 59-67.</li>
<li>Wanapat, M. and P. Rowlinson. 2007. Nutrition and feeding of swamp buffalo: Feed resources and rumen approach. Paper to be presented at the VIII World Buffalo Congress, 19–22 October 2007, Caserta, Italy, organized by The International Buffalo Federation.</li>
</ul>
